# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Producer RecordAccumulator Batch Drain Chain

## Your Task

Trace how Kafka producer records flow from ProducerRecord through the RecordAccumulator to the Sender thread in apache/kafka. Find Java source files implementing: the RecordAccumulator append, the batch ready check, the Sender drain, and the network send.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I've successfully completed the task. The answer file `/workspace/answer.json` has been created with a comprehensive trace of the Kafka producer record flow.

## Summary

I've traced the complete flow of records from `ProducerRecord` through the `RecordAccumulator` to the `Sender` thread and network send in apache/kafka:

**Key Components Identified:**

1. **ProducerRecord** - User's input record with topic, partition, key, value, and headers
2. **RecordAccumulator.append()** (lines 275-359) - Main accumulation method that batches records
3. **ProducerBatch.tryAppend()** (lines 144-163) - Appends individual records to batches
4. **RecordAccumulator.ready()** (lines 763-774) - Checks batch readiness via:
   - `partitionReady()` (lines 643-740) - Evaluates partitions with data
   - `batchReady()` (lines 603-627) - Determines if batch is ready based on fullness, linger time, or exhaustion
5. **RecordAccumulator.drain()** (lines 954-962) - Drains ready batches for sending
6. **Sender.run()** (lines 236-299) - Main sender thread loop

allocation blocked above.\\n335:                     // NOTE: getting time may be expensive, so calling it under a lock\\n336:                     // should be avoided.\\n337:                     nowMs = time.milliseconds();\\n338:                 }\\n339: \\n340:                 synchronized (dq) {\\n341:                     // After taking the lock, validate that the partition hasn't changed and retry.\\n342:                     if (partitionChanged(topic, topicInfo, partitionInfo, dq, nowMs, cluster))\\n343:                         continue;\\n344: \\n345: deallocate doesn't return it back to free pool, since it's used in the batch.\\n347:                     if (appendResult.newBatchCreated)\\n348:                         buffer = null;\\n349:                     // If queue has incomplete batches we disable switch (see comments in updatePartitionInfo).\\n350:                     boolean enableSwitch = allBatchesFull(dq);\\n351:                     topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionInfo(partitionInfo, appendResult.appendedBytes, cluster, enableSwitch);\\n352:                     return appendResult;\\n353:                 }\\n354:             }\\n355:         } finally {\\n356:             free.deallocate(buffer);\\n357:             appendsInProgress.decrementAndGet();\\n358:         }\\n359:     }\\n360: \\n361:     /**\\n362:      * Append a new batch to the queue\\n363:      *\\n364:      * @param topic The topic\\n365:      * @param partition The partition (cannot be RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION)\\n366:      * @param dq The queue\\n367:      * @param timestamp The timestamp of the record\\n368:      * @param key The key for the record\\n369:      * @param value The value for the record\\n370:      * @param headers the Headers for the record\\n371:      * @param callbacks The callbacks to execute\\n372:      * @param buffer The buffer for the new batch\\n373:      * @param nowMs The current time, in milliseconds\\n374:      */\\n375:     private RecordAppendResult appendNewBatch(String topic,\\n376:                                               int partition,\\n377:                                               Deque<ProducerBatch> dq,\\n378:                                               long timestamp,\\n379:                                               byte[] key,\\n380:                                               byte[] value,\\n381:                                               Header[] headers,\\n382:                                               AppendCallbacks callbacks,\\n383:                                               ByteBuffer buffer,\\n384:                                               long nowMs) {\\n385:         assert partition != RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION;\\n386: \\n387:         RecordAppendResult appendResult = tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callbacks, dq, nowMs);\\n388:         if (appendResult != null) {\\n389:             // Somebody else found us a batch, return the one we waited for! Hopefully this doesn't happen often...\\n390:             return appendResult;\\n391:         }\\n392: \\n393:         MemoryRecordsBuilder recordsBuilder = recordsBuilder(buffer);\\n394:         ProducerBatch batch = new ProducerBatch(new TopicPartition(topic, partition), recordsBuilder, nowMs);\\n395:         FutureRecordMetadata future = Objects.requireNonNull(batch.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers,\\n396:                 callbacks, nowMs));\\n397: \\n398:         dq.addLast(batch);\\n399:         incomplete.add(batch);\\n400: \\n401:         return new RecordAppendResult(future, dq.size() > 1 || batch.isFull(), true, batch.estimatedSizeInBytes());\\n402:     }\\n403: \\n404:     private MemoryRecordsBuilder recordsBuilder(ByteBuffer buffer) {\\n405:         return MemoryRecords.builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, TimestampType.CREATE_TIME, 0L);\\n406:     }\\n407: \\n408:     /**\\n409:      * Check if all batches in the queue are full.\\n410:      */\\n411:     private boolean allBatchesFull(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque) {\\n412:         // Only the last batch may be incomplete, so we just check that.\\n413:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\\n414:         return last == null || last.isFull();\\n415:     }\\n416: \\n417:      /**\\n418:      *  Try to append to a ProducerBatch.\\n419:      *\\n420:      *  If it is full, we return null and a new batch is created. We also close the batch for record appends to free up\\n421:      *  resources like compression buffers. The batch will be fully closed (ie. the record batch headers will be written\\n422:      *  and memory records built) in one of the following cases (whichever comes first): right before send,\\n423:      *  if it is expired, or when the producer is closed.\\n424:      */\\n425:     private RecordAppendResult tryAppend(long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers,\\n426:                                          Callback callback, Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, long nowMs) {\\n427:         if (closed)\\n428:             throw new KafkaException(\\\"Producer closed while send in progress\\\");\\n429:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\\n430:         if (last != null) {\\n431:             int initialBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes();\\n432:             FutureRecordMetadata future = last.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callback, nowMs);\\n433:             if (future == null) {\\n434:                 last.closeForRecordAppends();\\n435:             } else {\\n436:                 int appendedBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes() - initialBytes;\\n437:                 return new RecordAppendResult(future, deque.size() > 1 || last.isFull(), false, appendedBytes);\\n438:             }\\n439:         }\\n440:         return null;\\n441:     }\\n442: \\n443:     private boolean isMuted(TopicPartition tp) {\\n444:         return muted.contains(tp);\\n445:     }\\n446: \\n447:     public void resetNextBatchExpiryTime() {\\n448:         nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\\n449:     }\\n450: \\n451:     public void maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(ProducerBatch batch) {\\n452:         if (batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs  > 0) {\\n453:             // the non-negative check is to guard us against potential overflow due to setting\\n454:             // a large value for deliveryTimeoutMs\\n455:             nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Math.min(nextBatchExpiryTimeMs, batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs);\\n456:         } else {\\n457:             log.warn(\\\"Skipping next batch expiry time update due to addition overflow: \\\"\\n458:                 + \\\"batch.createMs={}, deliveryTimeoutMs={}\\\", batch.createdMs, deliveryTimeoutMs);\\n459:         }\\n460:     }\\n461: \\n462:     /**\\n463:      * Get a list of batches which have been sitting in the accumulator too long and need to be expired.\\n464:      */\\n465:     public List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches(long now) {\\n466:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = new ArrayList<>();\\n467:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\\n468:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\\n469:                 // expire the batches in the order of sending\\n470:                 synchronized (deque) {\\n471:                     while (!deque.isEmpty()) {\\n472:                         ProducerBatch batch = deque.getFirst();\\n473:                   expiredBatches.add(batch);\\n477:                         } else {\\n478:                             maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(batch);\\n479: In Sender.completeBatch method, we check\\n494:      * whether the batch has reached deliveryTimeoutMs or not. Hence we do not do the delivery timeout check here.\\n495:      */\\n496:     public void reenqueue(ProducerBatch batch, long now) {\\n497:         batch.reenqueued(now);\\n498:         Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getOrCreateDeque(batch.topicPartition);\\n499:         synchronized (deque) {\\n500:             if (transactionManager != null)\\n501:                 insertInSequenceOrder(deque, batch);\\n502:             else\\n503:                 deque.addFirst(batch);\\n504:         }\\n505:     }\\n506: \\n507:     /**\\n508:      * Split the big batch that has been rejected and reenqueue the split batches in to the accumulator.\\n509:      * @return the number of split batches.\\n510:      */\\n511:     public int splitAndReenqueue(ProducerBatch bigBatch) {\\n512:         // Reset the estimated compression ratio to the initial value or the big batch compression ratio, whichever\\n513:         // is bigger. There are several different ways to do the reset. We chose the most conservative one to ensure\\n514:         // the split doesn't happen too often.\\n515:         CompressionRatioEstimator.setEstimation(bigBatch.topicPartition.topic(), compression.type(),\\n516:                                                 Math.max(1.0f, (float) bigBatch.compressionRatio()));\\n517:         Deque<ProducerBatch> dq = bigBatch.split(this.batchSize);\\n518:         int numSplitBatches = dq.size();\\n519:         Deque<ProducerBatch> partitionDequeue = getOrCreateDeque(bigBatch.topicPartition);\\n520:         while (!dq.isEmpty()) {\\n521:             ProducerBatch batch = dq.pollLast();\\n522:             incomplete.add(batch);\\n523:             // We treat the newly split batches as if they are not even tried.\\n524:             synchronized (partitionDequeue) {\\n525:                 if (transactionManager != null) {\\n526:                     // We should track the newly created batches since they already have assigned sequences.\\n527:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\\n528:                     insertInSequenceOrder(partitionDequeue, batch);\\n529:                 } else {\\n530:                     partitionDequeue.addFirst(batch);\\n531:                 }\\n532:             }\\n533:         }\\n534:         return numSplitBatches;\\n535:     }\\n536: \\n537:     // We will have to do extra work to ensure the queue is in order when requests are being retried and there are\\n538:     // multiple requests in flight to that partition. If the first in flight request fails to append, then all the\\n539:     // subsequent in flight requests will also fail because the sequence numbers will not be accepted.\\n540:     //\\n541:     // Further, once batches are being retried, we are reduced to a single in flight request for that partition. So when\\n542:     // the subsequent batches come back in sequence order, they will have to be placed further back in the queue.\\n543:     //\\n544:     // Note that this assumes that all the batches in the queue which have an assigned sequence also have the current\\n545:     // producer id. We will not attempt to reorder messages if the producer id has changed, we will throw an\\n546:     // IllegalStateException instead.\\n547:     private void insertInSequenceOrder(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, ProducerBatch batch) {\\n548:         // When we are re-enqueueing and have enabled idempotence, the re-enqueued batch must always have a sequence.\\n549:         if (batch.baseSequence() == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\\n550:             throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"Trying to re-enqueue a batch which doesn't have a sequence even \\\" +\\n551:                 \\\"though idempotency is enabled.\\\");\\n552: \\n553:         if (!transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(batch.topicPartition))\\n554:             throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"We are re-enqueueing a batch which is not tracked as part of the in flight \\\" +\\n555:                 \\\"requests. batch.topicPartition: \\\" + batch.topicPartition + \\\"; It was placed in the queue at \\\" +\\n572:                 \\\"position {}\\\", batch.baseSequence(), batch.topicPartition, orderedBatches.size());\\n573:             // Either we have reached a point where there are batches without a sequence (ie. never been drained\\n574:             // and are hence in order by default), or the batch at the front of the queue has a sequence greater\\n575:             // than the incoming batch. This is the right place to add the incoming batch.\\n576:             deque.addFirst(batch);\\n577: \\n578:             // Now we have to re insert the previously queued batches in the right order.\\n579:             for (int i = orderedBatches.size() - 1; i >= 0; --i) {\\n580:                 deque.addFirst(orderedBatches.get(i));\\n581:             }\\n582: \\n583:             // At this point, the incoming batch has been queued in the correct place according to its sequence.\\n584:         } else {\\n585:             deque.addFirst(batch);\\n586:         }\\n587:     }\\n588: \\n589:     /**\\n590:      * Add the leader to the ready nodes if the batch is ready\\n591:      *\\n592:      * @param exhausted 'true' is the buffer pool is exhausted\\n593:      * @param part The partition\\n594:      * @param leader The leader for the partition\\n595:      * @param waitedTimeMs How long batch waited\\n596:      * @param backingOff Is backing off\\n597:      * @param backoffAttempts Number of attempts for calculating backoff delay\\n598:      * @param full Is batch full\\n599:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\\n600:      * @param readyNodes The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\\n601:      * @return The delay for next check\\n602:      */\\n603:     private long batchReady(boolean exhausted, TopicPartition part, Node leader,\\n604:                             long waitedTimeMs, boolean backingOff, int backoffAttempts,\\n605:                             boolean full, long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes) {\\n606:         if (!readyNodes.contains(leader) && !isMuted(part)) {\\n607:             long timeToWaitMs = backingOff ? retryBackoff.backoff(backoffAttempts > 0 ? backoffAttempts - 1 : 0) : lingerMs;\\n608:             boolean expired = waitedTimeMs >= timeToWaitMs;\\n609:             boolean transactionCompleting = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isCompleting();\\n610:             boolean sendable = full\\n611:                     || expired\\n612:                     || exhausted\\n613:                     || closed\\n614:                     || flushInProgress()\\n615:                     || transactionCompleting;\\n616:             if (sendable && !backingOff) {\\n617:                 readyNodes.add(leader);\\n618:             } else {\\n619:                 long timeLeftMs = Math.max(timeToWaitMs - waitedTimeMs, 0);\\n620:                 // Note that this results in a conservative estimate since an un-sendable partition may have\\n621:                 // a leader that will later be found to have sendable data. However, this is good enough\\n622:                 // since we'll just wake up and then sleep again for the remaining time.\\n623:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Math.min(timeLeftMs, nextReadyCheckDelayMs);\\n624:             }\\n625:         }\\n626:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\\n627:     }\\n628: \\n629:     /**\\n630:      * Iterate over partitions to see which one have batches ready and collect leaders of those\\n631:      * partitions into the set of ready nodes. The reason is that we build queue sizes from the batches map,\\n654:             // and if an entry is missing in the batches map, then adaptive partitioning logic\\n655:             // won't know about it and won't switch to it.\\n656:             queueSizes = new int[batches.size()];\\n657:             partitionIds = new int[queueSizes.length];\\n658:         }\\n659: \\n660:         int queueSizesIndex = -1;\\n661:         boolean exhausted = this.free.queued() > 0;\\n662:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> entry : batches.entrySet()) {\\n663:             TopicPartition part = new TopicPartition(topic, entry.getKey());\\n664:             // Advance queueSizesIndex so that we properly index available\\n665:             // partitions.  Do it here so that it's done for all code paths.\\n666: \\n667:             Node leader = metadataSnapshot.cluster().leaderFor(part);\\n668:             if (leader != null && queueSizes != null) {\\n669:                 ++queueSizesIndex;\\n670:                 assert queueSizesIndex < queueSizes.length;\\n671:                 partitionIds[queueSizesIndex] = part.partition();\\n672:             }\\n673: \\n674:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = entry.getValue();\\n675: \\n676:             final long waitedTimeMs;\\n677:             final boolean backingOff;\\n678:             final int backoffAttempts;\\n679:             final int dequeSize;\\n680:             final boolean full;\\n681: \\n682:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(part);\\n683: \\n684:             // This loop is especially hot with large partition counts. So -\\n685: \\n686:             // 1. We should avoid code that increases synchronization between application thread calling\\n687:             // send(), and background thread running runOnce(), see https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16226\\n688: \\n689:             // 2. We are careful to only perform the minimum required inside the\\n690:             // synchronized block, as this lock is also used to synchronize producer threads\\n691:             // attempting to append() to a partition/batch.\\n692: \\n693:             synchronized (deque) {\\n694:                 // Deques are often empty in this path, esp with large partition counts,\\n695:                 // so we exit early if we can.\\n696:                 ProducerBatch batch = deque.peekFirst();\\n697:                 if (batch == null) {\\n698:                     continue;\\n699:                 }\\n700: \\n701:                 waitedTimeMs = batch.waitedTimeMs(nowMs);\\n702:                 batch.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\\n703:                 backingOff =           full = dequeSize > 1 || batch.isFull();\\n707:             }\\n708: \\n709:             if (leader == null) {\\n710:                 // This is a partition for which leader is not known, but messages are available to send.\\n711:                 // Note that entries are currently not removed from batches when deque is empty.\\n712:                 unknownLeaderTopics.add(part.topic());\\n713:             } else {\\n714:                 if (queueSizes != null)\\n715:                     queueSizes[queueSizesIndex] = dequeSize;\\n716:                 if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs > 0) {\\n717:                     // Check if we want to exclude the partition from the list of available partitions\\n718:                     // if the broker hasn't responded for some time.\\n719:                     NodeLatencyStats nodeLatencyStats = nodeStats.get(leader.id());\\n720:                     if (nodeLatencyStats != null) {\\n721:                         // NOTE: there is no synchronization between reading metrics,\\n722:                         // so we read ready time first to avoid accidentally marking partition\\n723:                         // unavailable if we read while the metrics are being updated.\\n724:                         long readyTimeMs = nodeLatencyStats.readyTimeMs;\\n725:                         if (readyTimeMs - nodeLatencyStats.drainTimeMs > partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs)\\n726:                             --queueSizesIndex;\\n727:                     }\\n728:                 }\\n729: \\n730:         }\\n734: \\n735:         // We've collected the queue sizes for partitions of this topic, now we can calculate\\n736:         // load stats. queueSizesIndex + 1);\\n739:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\\n740:     }\\n741: \\n742:     /**\\n743:      * Get a list of nodes whose partitions are ready to be sent, and the earliest time at which any non-sendable\\n744:      * partition will be ready; Also return the flag for whether there are any unknown leaders for the accumulated\\n745:      * partition batches.\\n746:      * <p>\\n747:      * A destination node is ready to send data if:\\n748:      * <ol>\\n749:      * <li>There is at least one partition that is not backing off its send\\n750:      * <li><b>and</b> those partitions are not muted (to prevent reordering if\\n751:      *   {@value org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.ProducerConfig#MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION}\\n752:      *   is set to are immediately considered ready).</li>\\n759:      *     <li>The accumulator has been closed</li>\\n760:      * </ul>\\n761:      * </ol>\\n762:      */\\n763:     public ReadyCheckResult ready(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs) {\\n764:         Set<Node> readyNodes = new HashSet<>();\\n765:         long nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\\n766:         Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics = new HashSet<>();\\n767:         // Go topic by topic so that we can get queue sizes for partitions in a topic and calculate\\n768:         // cumulative frequency table (used in partitioner).\\n769:         for (Map.Entry<String, TopicInfo> topicInfoEntry : this.topicInfoMap.entrySet()) {\\n770:             final String topic = topicInfoEntry.getKey();\\n771: ReadyCheckResult(readyNodes, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, unknownLeaderTopics);\\n774:     }\\n775: \\n776:     /**\\n777:      * Check whether there are any batches which haven't been drained\\n778:      */\\n779:     public boolean hasUndrained() {\\n780:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\\n781:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\\n782:                 synchronized (deque) {\\n783:                     if (!deque.isEmpty())\\n784:                         return true;\\n785:                 }\\n786:             }\\n787:         }\\n788:         return false;\\n789:     }\\n790: \\n791:     private boolean shouldBackoff(boolean hasLeaderChanged, final ProducerBatch batch, final long waitedTimeMs) {\\n792:         boolean shouldWaitMore = batch.attempts() > 0 && waitedTimeMs < retryBackoff.backoff(batch.attempts() - 1);\\n793:         boolean shouldBackoff = !hasLeaderChanged && shouldWaitMore;\\n794:         if (log.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n795:             if (shouldBackoff) {\\n796:                 log.trace(\\n797:                     \\\"For {}, will backoff\\\", batch);\\n798:             } else {\\n799:                 log.trace(\\n800:                     \\\"For {}, will not backoff, shouldWaitMore {}, hasLeaderChanged {}\\\", batch,\\n801:                     shouldWaitMore, hasLeaderChanged);\\n802:             }\\n803:         } else if (log.isDebugEnabled() && hasLeaderChanged) {\\n804:             // Add less-verbose log at DEBUG.\\n805:             log.debug(\\\"For {}, leader has changed, hence skipping backoff.\\\", batch);\\n806:         }\\n807:         return shouldBackoff;\\n808:     }\\n809: \\n810:     private boolean shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(ProducerBatch first, TopicPartition tp) {\\n811:         ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch;\\n812:         if (transactionManager != null) {\\n813:             if (!transactionManager.isSendToPartitionAllowed(tp))\\n814:                 return true;\\n815: \\n816:             producerIdAndEpoch = transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch();\\n817:             if (!producerIdAndEpoch.isValid())\\n818:                 // we cannot send the batch until we have refreshed the producer id\\n819:                 return true;\\n820: \\n821:             if (!first.hasSequence()) {\\n822:                 if (transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(tp) && transactionManager.hasStaleProducerIdAndEpoch(tp)) {\\n823:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the partition has in-flight batches with a different epoch\\n824:                     // and/or producer ID. Otherwise, a batch with a new epoch and sequence number\\n825:                     // 0 could be written before earlier batches complete, which would cause out of sequence errors\\n826:                     return true;\\n827:                 }\\n828: \\n829:                 if (transactionManager.hasUnresolvedSequence(first.topicPartition))\\n830:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the state of previous sequence numbers\\n831:                     // is unknown. The previous batches would be unknown if they were aborted\\n832:                     // on the client after being sent to the broker at least once.\\n833:                     return true;\\n834:             }\\n835: \\n836:             int firstInFlightSequence = transactionManager.firstInFlightSequence(first.topicPartition);\\n837:             // If the queued batch already has an assigned sequence, then it is being retried.\\n838:             // In this case, we wait until the next immediate batch is ready and drain that.\\n839:             // We only move on when the next in line batch is complete (either successfully or due to\\n840:             // a fatal broker error). This effectively reduces our in flight request count to 1.\\n841:             return firstInFlightSequence != RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE && first.hasSequence()\\n842:                     && first.baseSequence() != firstInFlightSequence;\\n843:         }\\n844:         return false;\\n845:     }\\n846: \\n847:     private List<ProducerBatch> drainBatchesForOneNode(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Node node, int maxSize, long now) {\\n848:         int size = 0;\\n849:         List<PartitionInfo> parts = metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForNode(node.id());\\n850:         List<ProducerBatch> ready = new ArrayList<>();\\n851:         if (parts.isEmpty())\\n852:             return ready;\\n853:         /* to make starvation less likely each node has it's own drainIndex */\\n854:         int drainIndex = getDrainIndex(node.idString());\\n855:         int start = drainIndex = drainIndex % parts.size();\\n856:         do {\\n857:             PartitionInfo part = parts.get(drainIndex);\\n858: \\n859:             TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(part.topic(), part.partition());\\n860:             updateDrainIndex(node.idString(), drainIndex);\\n861:             drainIndex = (drainIndex + 1) % parts.size();\\n862:             // Only proceed if the partition has no in-flight batches.\\n863:             if (isMuted(tp))\\n864:                 continue;\\n865:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getDeque(tp);\\n866:             if (deque == null)\\n867:                 continue;\\n868: \\n869:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(tp);\\n870: \\n871:             final ProducerBatch batch;\\n872:             synchronized (deque) {\\n873:                 // invariant: !isMuted(tp,now) && deque != null\\n874:                 ProducerBatch first = deque.peekFirst();\\n875:                 if (first == null)\\n876:                     continue;\\n877: \\n878:                 // first != null\\n879:                 // Only drain the batch if it is not during backoff period.\\n880:                 first.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\\n881:                 if (shouldBackoff(first.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), first, first.waitedTimeMs(now)))\\n882:                     continue;\\n883: \\n884:                 if (size + first.estimatedSizeInBytes() > maxSize && !ready.isEmpty()) {\\n885:                     // there is a rare case that a single batch size is larger than the request size due to\\n886:                     // compression; in this case we will still eventually send this batch in a single request\\n887:                     break;\\n888:                 } else {\\n889:                     if (shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(first, tp))\\n890:                         break;\\n891:                 }\\n892: \\n893:                 batch = deque.pollFirst();\\n894: \\n895:                 boolean isTransactional = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isTransactional();\\n896:                 ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch =\\n897:                     transactionManager != null ? transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch() : null;\\n898:                 if (producerIdAndEpoch != null && !batch.hasSequence()) {\\n899:                     // If the producer id/epoch of the partition do not match the latest one\\n900:                     // of the producer, we update it and reset the sequence. This should be\\n901:                     // only done when all its in-flight batches have completed. This is guarantee\\n902:                     // in `shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition`.\\n903:                     transactionManager.maybeUpdateProducerIdAndEpoch(batch.topicPartition);\\n904: \\n905:                     // If the batch already has an assigned sequence, then we should not change the producer id and\\n906:                     // sequence number, since this may introduce duplicates. In particular, the previous attempt\\n907:                     // may actually have been accepted, and if we change the producer id and sequence here, this\\n908:                     // attempt will also be accepted, causing a duplicate.\\n909:                     //\\n910:                     // Additionally, we update the next sequence number bound for the partition, and also have\\n911:                     // the transaction manager track the batch so as to ensure that sequence ordering is maintained\\n912:                     // even if we receive out of order responses.\\n913:                     batch.setProducerState(producerIdAndEpoch, transactionManager.sequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition), isTransactional);\\n914:                     transactionManager.incrementSequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition, batch.recordCount);\\n915:                     log.debug(\\\"Assigned producerId {} and producerEpoch {} to batch with base sequence \\\" +\\n916:                             \\\"{} being sent to partition {}\\\", producerIdAndEpoch.producerId,\\n917:                         producerIdAndEpoch.epoch, batch.baseSequence(), tp);\\n918: \\n919:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\\n920:                 }\\n921:             }\\n922: \\n923:             // the rest of the work by processing outside the lock\\n924:             // close() is particularly expensive\\n925:             batch.close();\\n926:             size += batch.records().sizeInBytes();\\n927:             ready.add(batch);\\n928: \\n929:             batch.drained(now);\\n930:         } while (start != drainIndex);\\n931:         return ready;\\n932:     }\\n933: \\n934:     private int {\\n939:         nodesDrainIndex.put(idString, drainIndex);\\n940:     }\\n941: \\n942:     /**\\n943:      * Drain all the data for the given nodes and collate them into a list of batches that will       (config, now) -> free.availableMemory());\n213:     }\n214: \n215:     private void setPartition(AppendCallbacks callbacks, int partition) {\n216:         if (callbacks != null)\n217: *\n223:      * @param topic The topic\n224:      * @param topicInfo The topic info\n225:      * @param partitionInfo The built-in partitioner's partition info\n226:      * @param deque The partition info and retry,\n230:      *         'false' otherwise\n231:      */\n232:     private boolean partitionChanged(String topic,\n233:                                      TopicInfo topicInfo,\n234:                                      BuiltInPartitioner.StickyPartitionInfo partitionInfo,\n235:                                      Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, long nowMs,\n236:                                      Cluster cluster) {\n237:         if (topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.isPartitionChanged(partitionInfo)) {\n238:             log.trace(\"Partition {} for topic {} switched by a concurrent      }\n252:         }\n253: \n254:         return false;\n255:     }\n256: \n257:     /**\n258:      * Add a record to the accumulator, return the append result\n259:      * <p>\n260:      * The this record is being sent\n264:      * @param partition The partition to which this record is being sent or RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION\n265:      *                  if any partition could be used\n266:      * @param timestamp The timestamp of the record\n267:      * @param key The key for the record\n268:      * @param value The value for the record\n269:      * @param headers the Headers for the record\n270:      * @param callbacks The callbacks to execute\n271:      * @param maxTimeToBlock The maximum time in milliseconds to block for buffer memory to be available\n272:      * @param nowMs The current time, in milliseconds\n273:      * @param cluster The cluster metadata\n274:      */\n275:     public RecordAppendResult append(String topic,\n276:                                      int partition,\n277:                                      long timestamp,\n278:                                      byte[] key,\n279:                                      byte[] value,\n280:                                      Header[] headers,\n281:                                      AppendCallbacks callbacks,\n282:                                      long maxTimeToBlock,\n283:                                      long nowMs,\n284:                                      Cluster cluster) throws InterruptedException {\n285:         TopicInfo topicInfo = topicInfoMap.computeIfAbsent(topic, k -> new TopicInfo(createBuiltInPartitioner(logContext, k, batchSize)));\n286: \n287:         // We keep track of the number of appending thread to make sure we do not miss batches in\n288:         // abortIncompleteBatches().\n289:         appendsInProgress.incrementAndGet();\n290:         ByteBuffer buffer = null;\n291:         if (headers == null) headers = Record.EMPTY_HEADERS;\n292:         try {\n293:             // Loop to retry in case we encounter partitioner's race conditions.\n294:             while (true) {\n295:                 // If the message doesn't have any partition affinity, so we pick a partition based on the broker\n296:                 // availability and performance.  Note, that here we peek current partition before we hold the\n297:                 // deque lock, so we'll need to make sure that it's not changed while we were waiting for the\n298:                 // deque lock.\n299:                 final BuiltInPartitioner.StickyPartitionInfo partitionInfo;\n300:                 final int effectivePartition;\n301:                 if (partition == RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION) {\n302:                     partitionInfo = topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.peekCurrentPartitionInfo(cluster);\n303:                     effectivePartition = partitionInfo.partition();\n304:                 } else {\n305:                     partitionInfo = null;\n306:                     effectivePartition = partition;\n307:                 }\n308: \n309:                 // Now that we know the effective partition, let the caller know.\n310:                 setPartition(callbacks, effectivePartition);\n311: \n312:                 // check if we have an in-progress batch\n313:                 Deque<ProducerBatch> dq = topicInfo.batches.computeIfAbsent(effectivePartition, k -> new ArrayDeque<>());\n314:                 synchronized (dq) {\n315:                     // After taking the lock, validate that the partition hasn't changed and retry.\n316:                     if (partitionChanged(topic, topicInfo, partitionInfo, dq, nowMs, cluster))\n317:                         continue;\n318: \n319:                     RecordAppendResult appendResult = tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callbacks, dq, nowMs);\n320:                     if (appendResult != null) {\n321:                         // If queue has incomplete batches we disable switch (see comments in updatePartitionInfo).\n322:                         boolean enableSwitch = allBatchesFull(dq);\n323:                         topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionInfo(partitionInfo, appendResult.appendedBytes, cluster, enableSwitch);\n324:                         return appendResult;\n325:                     }\n326:                 }\n327: \n328:                 if (buffer == null) {\n329:                     int size = Math.max(this.batchSize, AbstractRecords.estimateSizeInBytesUpperBound(\n330:                             RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression.type(), key, value, headers));\n331:                     log.trace(\"Allocating a new {} byte message buffer for topic {} partition {} with remaining timeout {}ms\", size, topic, effectivePartition, maxTimeToBlock);\n332:                     // This call may block if we exhausted buffer space.\n333:                     buffer = free.allocate(size, maxTimeToBlock);\n334:                     // Update the current time in case the buffer allocation blocked above.\n335:                     // NOTE: getting time may be expensive, so calling it under a lock\n336:                     // should be avoided.\n337:                     nowMs = time.milliseconds();\n338:                 }\n339: \n340:                 synchronized (dq) {\n341:                     // After taking the lock, validate that the partition hasn't changed and retry.\n342:                     if (partitionChanged(topic, topicInfo, partitionInfo, dq, nowMs, cluster))\n343:                         continue;\n344: \n345:                     RecordAppendResult appendResult = appendNewBatch(topic, effectivePartition, dq, timestamp, key, value, headers, callbacks, buffer, nowMs);\n346:                     // Set buffer to null, so that deallocate doesn't topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionInfo(partitionInfo, appendResult.appendedBytes, cluster, enableSwitch);\n352:                     return appendResult;\n353:                 }\n354:             }\n355:         } finally {\n356:             free.deallocate(buffer);\n357:             appendsInProgress.decrementAndGet();\n358:         }\n359:     }\n360: \n361:     /**\n362:      * Append a new batch to the queue\n363:      *\n364:      * @param topic The topic\n365:      * @param partition The partition (cannot be RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION)\n366:      * @param dq The queue\n367:      * @param timestamp The timestamp of the record\n368:      * @param key The key for the record\n369:      * @param value The value for the record\n370:      * @param headers the Headers for the record\n371:      * @param callbacks The callbacks to execute\n372:      * @param buffer The buffer for the new batch\n373:      * @param nowMs The current time, in milliseconds\n374:      */\n375: dq,\n378:                                               long timestamp,\n379:                                               byte[] key,\n380:                                               byte[] value,\n381:                                               Header[] headers,\n382:                                               AppendCallbacks callbacks,\n383:                                               ByteBuffer buffer,\n384:                                               long nowMs) {\n385:         assert partition != RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION;\n386: \n387:         RecordAppendResult appendResult = tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callbacks, dq, nowMs);\n388:         if (appendResult != null) {\n389:             // Somebody else found us a batch, return the one we waited for! Hopefully this doesn't happen often...\n390:             return appendResult;\n391:         }\n392: \n393:         MemoryRecordsBuilder recordsBuilder = recordsBuilder(buffer);\n394:         ProducerBatch batch = new ProducerBatch(new TopicPartition(topic, partition), recordsBuilder, nowMs);\n395:         FutureRecordMetadata future = Objects.requireNonNull(batch.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers,\n396:                 callbacks, nowMs));\n397: \n398:         dq.addLast(batch);\n399:         incomplete.add(batch);\n400: \n401:         return new RecordAppendResult(future, dq.size() > 1 || batch.isFull(), true, batch.estimatedSizeInBytes());\n402:     }\n403: \n404:     private MemoryRecordsBuilder recordsBuilder(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n405:         return MemoryRecords.builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, TimestampType.CREATE_TIME, 0L);\n406:     }\n407: \n408:     /**\n409:      * Check if all batches in the queue are full.\n410:      */\n411:     private boolean allBatchesFull(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque) {\n412:         // Only the last batch may be incomplete, so we just check that.\n413:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\n414:         return last == null || last.isFull();\n415:     }\n416: \n417:      /**\n418:      *  Try to append to a ProducerBatch.\n419:      *\n420:      *  If it is full, we return null and a new batch is created. We also close the batch for record appends to free up\n421:      *  resources like compression buffers. The batch will be fully closed (ie. the record batch headers will be written\n422:      *  and memory records built) in one of the following cases (whichever comes first): right before send,\n423:      *  if it is expired, or when the producer is closed.\n424:      */\n425:     private RecordAppendResult tryAppend(long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers,\n426:                                          Callback callback, Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, long nowMs) {\n427:         if (closed)\n428:             throw new KafkaException(\"Producer closed while send in progress\");\n429:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\n430:         if (last != null) {\n431:             int initialBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes();\n432:             FutureRecordMetadata future = last.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callback, nowMs);\n433:             if (future == null) {\n434:                 last.closeForRecordAppends();\n435:             } else {\n436:                 int appendedBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes() - initialBytes;\n437:                 return new RecordAppendResult(future, deque.size() > 1 || last.isFull(), false, appendedBytes);\n438:             }\n439:         }\n440:         return null;\n441:     }\n442: \n443:     private boolean isMuted(TopicPartition tp) {\n444:         return muted.contains(tp);\n445:     }\n446: \n447:     public void resetNextBatchExpiryTime() {\n448:         nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n449:     }\n450: \n451:     public void maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(ProducerBatch batch) {\n452:         if (batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs  > 0) {\n453:             // the non-negative check is to guard us against potential overflow due to setting\n454:             // a large value for deliveryTimeoutMs\n455:             nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Math.min(nextBatchExpiryTimeMs, batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs);\n456:         } else {\n457:             log.warn(\"Skipping next batch expiry time update due to addition overflow: \"\n458:                 + \"batch.createMs={}, deliveryTimeoutMs={}\", batch.createdMs, deliveryTimeoutMs);\n459:         }\n460:     }\n461: \n462:     /**\n463:      * Get a list of batches which have been sitting in the accumulator too long and need to be expired.\n464:      */\n465:     public List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches(long now) {\n466:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = new ArrayList<>();\n467:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\n468:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\n469:                 // expire the batches in the order of sending\n470:                 synchronized (deque) {\n471:                     while (!deque.isEmpty()) {\n472:                         ProducerBatch batch = deque.getFirst();\n473:                         if (batch.hasReachedDeliveryTimeout(deliveryTimeoutMs, now)) {\n474:                             deque.poll();\n475:                             batch.abortRecordAppends();\n476:                             expiredBatches.add(batch);\n477:                         } else {\n478:                             maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(batch);\n479:                             break;\n480:                         }\n481:                     }\n482:                 }\n483:             }\n484:         }\n485:         return expiredBatches;\n486:     }\n487: \n488:     public long getDeliveryTimeoutMs() {\n489:         return deliveryTimeoutMs;\n490:     }\n491: \n492:     /**\n493:      * Re-enqueue the given record batch in the accumulator. In Sender.completeBatch method, we check\n494:      * whether the batch has reached deliveryTimeoutMs or not. Hence we do not do the delivery timeout check here.\n495:      */\n496:     public void reenqueue(ProducerBatch batch, long now) {\n497:         batch.reenqueued(now);\n498:         Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getOrCreateDeque(batch.topicPartition);\n499:         synchronized (deque) {\n500:             if (transactionManager != null)\n501:                 insertInSequenceOrder(deque, batch);\n502:             else\n503:                 deque.addFirst(batch);\n504:         }\n505:     }\n506: \n507:     /**\n508:      * Split the big batch that has been rejected and reenqueue the split batches in to the accumulator.\n509:      * @return the number of split batches.\n510:      */\n511:     public int splitAndReenqueue(ProducerBatch bigBatch) {\n512:         // Reset the estimated compression ratio to the initial value or the big batch compression ratio, whichever\n513:         // is bigger. There are several different ways to do the reset. We chose the most conservative one to ensure\n514:         // the split doesn't happen too often.\n515:         CompressionRatioEstimator.setEstimation(bigBatch.topicPartition.topic(), compression.type(),\n516:                                                 Math.max(1.0f, (float) bigBatch.compressionRatio()));\n517:         Deque<ProducerBatch> dq = bigBatch.split(this.batchSize);\n518:         int numSplitBatches = dq.size();\n519:         Deque<ProducerBatch> partitionDequeue = getOrCreateDeque(bigBatch.topicPartition);\n520:         while (!dq.isEmpty()) {\n521:             ProducerBatch batch = dq.pollLast();\n522:             incomplete.add(batch);\n523:             // We treat the newly split batches as if they are not even tried.\n524:             synchronized (partitionDequeue) {\n525:                 if (transactionManager != null) {\n526:                     // We should track the newly created batches since they already have assigned sequences.\n527:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\n528:                     insertInSequenceOrder(partitionDequeue, batch);\n529:                 } else {\n530:                     partitionDequeue.addFirst(batch);\n531:                 }\n532:             }\n533:         }\n534:         return numSplitBatches;\n535:     }\n536: \n537:     // We will have to do extra work to ensure the queue is in order when requests are being retried and there are\n538:     // multiple requests in flight to that partition. If the first in flight request fails to append, then all the\n539:     // subsequent in flight requests will also fail because the sequence numbers will not be accepted.\n540:     //\n541:     // Further, once batches are being retried, we are reduced to a single in flight request for that partition. So when\n542:     // the subsequent batches come back in sequence order, they will have to be placed further back in the queue.\n543:     //\n544:     // Note that this assumes that all the batches in the queue which have an assigned sequence also have the current\n545:     // producer id. We will not attempt to reorder messages if the producer id has changed, we will throw an\n546:     // IllegalStateException instead.\n547:     private void insertInSequenceOrder(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, ProducerBatch batch) {\n548:         // When we are re-enqueueing and have enabled idempotence, the re-enqueued batch must always have a sequence.\n549:         if (batch.baseSequence() == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\n550:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"Trying to re-enqueue a batch which doesn't have a sequence even \" +\n551:                 \"though idempotency is enabled.\");\n552: \n553:         if (!transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(batch.topicPartition))\n554:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"We are re-enqueueing a batch which is not tracked as part of the in flight \" +\n555:                 \"requests. batch.topicPartition: \" + batch.topicPartition + \"; batch.baseSequence: \" + batch.baseSequence());\n556: \n557:         ProducerBatch firstBatchInQueue = deque.peekFirst();\n558:         if (firstBatchInQueue != null && firstBatchInQueue.hasSequence() && firstBatchInQueue.baseSequence() < batch.baseSequence()) {\n559:             // The incoming batch can't be inserted at the front of the queue without violating the sequence ordering.\n560:             // This means that the incoming batch should be placed somewhere further back.\n561:             // We need to find the right place for the incoming batch and insert it there.\n562:             // We will only enter this branch if we have multiple inflights sent to different brokers and we need to retry\n563:             // the inflight batches.\n564:             //\n565:             // Since we reenqueue exactly one batch a time and ensure that the queue is ordered by sequence always, it\n566:             // is a simple linear scan of a subset of the in flight batches to find the right place in the queue each time.\n567:             List<ProducerBatch> orderedBatches = new ArrayList<>();\n568:             while (deque.peekFirst() != null && deque.peekFirst().hasSequence() && deque.peekFirst().baseSequence() < batch.baseSequence())\n569:                 orderedBatches.add(deque.pollFirst());\n570: \n571:             log.debug(\"Reordered incoming batch with sequence {} for partition {}. It was placed in the queue at \" +\n572:                 \"position {}\", batch.baseSequence(), batch.topicPartition, orderedBatches.size());\n573:             // Either we have reached a point where there are batches without a sequence (ie. never been drained\n574:             // and are hence in order by default), or the batch at the front of the queue has a sequence greater\n575:             // than the incoming batch. This is the right place to add the incoming batch.\n576:             deque.addFirst(batch);\n577: \n578:             // Now we have to re insert the previously queued batches in the right order.\n579:             for (int i = orderedBatches.size() - 1; i >= 0; --i) {\n580:                 deque.addFirst(orderedBatches.get(i));\n581:             }\n582: \n583:             // At this point, the incoming batch has been queued in the correct place according to its sequence.\n584:         } else {\n585:             deque.addFirst(batch);\n586:         }\n587:     }\n588: \n589:     /**\n590:      * Add the leader to the ready nodes if the batch is ready\n591:      *\n592:      * @param exhausted 'true' is the buffer pool is exhausted\n593:      * @param part The partition\n594:      * @param leader The leader for the partition\n595:      * @param waitedTimeMs How long batch waited\n596:      * @param backingOff Is backing off\n597:      * @param backoffAttempts Number of attempts for calculating backoff delay\n598:      * @param full Is batch full\n599:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\n600:      * @param readyNodes The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\n601:      * @return The delay for next check\n602:      */\n603:     private long batchReady(boolean exhausted, TopicPartition part, Node leader,\n604:                             long waitedTimeMs, boolean backingOff, int backoffAttempts,\n605:                             boolean full, long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes) {\n606:         if (!readyNodes.contains(leader) && !isMuted(part)) {\n607:             long timeToWaitMs = backingOff ? retryBackoff.backoff(backoffAttempts > 0 ? backoffAttempts - 1 : 0) : lingerMs;\n608:             boolean expired = waitedTimeMs >= timeToWaitMs;\n609:             boolean transactionCompleting = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isCompleting();\n610:             boolean sendable = full\n611:                     || expired\n612:                     || exhausted\n613:                     || closed\n614:                     || flushInProgress()\n615:                     || transactionCompleting;\n616:             if (sendable && !backingOff) {\n617:                 readyNodes.add(leader);\n618:             } else {\n619:                 long timeLeftMs = Math.max(timeToWaitMs - waitedTimeMs, 0);\n620:                 // Note that this results in a conservative estimate since an un-sendable partition may have\n621:                 // a leader that will later be found to have sendable data. However, this is good enough\n622:                 // since we'll just wake up and then sleep again for the remaining time.\n623:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Math.min(timeLeftMs, nextReadyCheckDelayMs);\n624:             }\n625:         }\n626:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\n627:     }\n628: \n629:     /**\n630:      * Iterate over partitions to see which one have batches ready and collect leaders of those\n631:      * partitions into the set of ready nodes.  If partition has no leader, add the topic to the set\n632:      * of topics with no leader.  This function also calculates stats for adaptive partitioning.\n633:      *\n634:      * @param metadataSnapshot      The cluster metadata\n635:      * @param nowMs                 The current time\n636:      * @param topic                 The topic\n637:      * @param topicInfo             The topic info\n638:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\n639:      * @param readyNodes            The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\n640:      * @param unknownLeaderTopics   The set of topics with no leader (to be filled in)\n641:      * @return The delay for next check\n642:      */\n643:     private long partitionReady(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs, String topic,\n644:                                 TopicInfo topicInfo,\n645:                                 long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes, Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics) {\n646:         ConcurrentMap<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> batches = topicInfo.batches;\n647:         // Collect the queue sizes for available partitions to be used in adaptive partitioning.\n648:         int[] queueSizes = null;\n649:         int[] partitionIds = null;\n650:         if (enableAdaptivePartitioning && batches.size() >= metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForTopic(topic).size()) {\n651:             // We don't do adaptive partitioning until we scheduled at least a batch for all\n652:             // partitions (i.e. we have the corresponding entries in the batches map), we just\n653:             // do uniform.  The reason is that we build queue sizes from the batches map,\n654:             // and if an entry is missing in the batches map, then adaptive partitioning logic\n655:             // won't know about it and won't switch to it.\n656:             queueSizes = new int[batches.size()];\n657:             partitionIds = new int[queueSizes.length];\n658:         }\n659: \n660:         int queueSizesIndex = -1;\n661:         boolean exhausted = this.free.queued() > 0;\n662:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> entry : batches.entrySet()) {\n663:             TopicPartition part = new TopicPartition(topic, entry.getKey());\n664:             // Advance queueSizesIndex so that we properly index available\n665:             // partitions.  Do it here so that it's done for all code paths.\n666: \n667:             Node leader = metadataSnapshot.cluster().leaderFor(part);\n668:             if (leader != null && queueSizes != null) {\n669:                 ++queueSizesIndex;\n670:                 assert queueSizesIndex < queueSizes.length;\n671:                 partitionIds[queueSizesIndex] = part.partition();\n672:             }\n673: \n674:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = entry.getValue();\n675: \n676:             final long waitedTimeMs;\n677:             final boolean backingOff;\n678:             final int backoffAttempts;\n679:             final int dequeSize;\n680:             final boolean full;\n681: \n682:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(part);\n683: \n684:             // This loop is especially hot with large partition counts. So -\n685: \n686:             // 1. We should avoid code that increases synchronization between application thread calling\n687:             // send(), and background thread running runOnce(), see https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16226\n688: \n689:             // 2. We are careful to only perform the minimum required inside the\n690:             // synchronized block, as this lock is also used to synchronize producer threads\n691:             // attempting to append() to a partition/batch.\n692: \n693:             synchronized (deque) {\n694:                 // Deques are often empty in this path, esp with large partition counts,\n695:                 // so we exit early if we can.\n696:                 ProducerBatch batch = deque.peekFirst();\n697:                 if (batch == null) {\n698:                     continue;\n699:                 }\n700: \n701:                 waitedTimeMs = batch.waitedTimeMs(nowMs);\n702:                 batch.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\n703:                 backingOff = shouldBackoff(batch.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), batch, waitedTimeMs);\n704:                 backoffAttempts = batch.attempts();\n705:                 dequeSize = deque.size();\n706:                 full = dequeSize > 1 || batch.isFull();\n707:             }\n708: \n709:             if (leader == null) {\n710:                 // This is a partition for which leader is not known, but messages are available to send.\n711:                 // Note that entries are currently not removed from batches when deque is empty.\n712:                 unknownLeaderTopics.add(part.topic());\n713:             } else {\n714:                 if (queueSizes != null)\n715:                     queueSizes[queueSizesIndex] = dequeSize;\n716:                 if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs > 0) {\n717:                     // Check if we want to exclude the partition from the list of available partitions\n718:                     // if the broker hasn't responded for some time.\n719:                     NodeLatencyStats nodeLatencyStats = nodeStats.get(leader.id());\n720:                     if (nodeLatencyStats != null) {\n721:                         // NOTE: there is no synchronization between reading metrics,\n722:                         // so we read ready time first to avoid accidentally marking partition\n723:                         // unavailable if we read while the metrics are being updated.\n724:                         long readyTimeMs = nodeLatencyStats.readyTimeMs;\n725:                         if (readyTimeMs - nodeLatencyStats.drainTimeMs > partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs)\n726:                             --queueSizesIndex;\n727:                     }\n728:                 }\n729: \n730:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = batchReady(exhausted, part, leader, waitedTimeMs, backingOff,\n731:                     backoffAttempts, full, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, readyNodes);\n732:             }\n733:         }\n734: \n735:         // We've collected the queue sizes for partitions of this topic, now we can calculate\n736:         // load stats.  NOTE: the stats are calculated in place, modifying the\n737:         // queueSizes array.\n738:         topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionLoadStats(queueSizes, partitionIds, queueSizesIndex + 1);\n739:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\n740:     }\n741: \n742:     /**\n743:      * Get a list of nodes whose partitions are ready to be sent, and the earliest time at which any non-sendable\n744:      * partition will be ready; Also return the flag for whether there are any unknown leaders for the accumulated\n745:      * partition batches.\n746:      * <p>\n747:      * A destination node is ready to send data if:\n748:      * <ol>\n749:      * <li>There is at least one partition that is not backing off its send\n750:      * <li><b>and</b> those partitions are not muted (to prevent reordering if\n751:      *   {@value org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.ProducerConfig#MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION}\n752:      *   is set to one)</li>\n753:      * <li><b>and <i>any</i></b> of the following are true</li>\n754:      * <ul>\n755:      *     <li>The record set is full</li>\n756:      *     <li>The record set has sat in the accumulator for at least lingerMs milliseconds</li>\n757:      *     <li>The accumulator is out of memory and threads are blocking waiting for data (in this case all partitions\n758:      *     are immediately considered ready).</li>\n759:      *     <li>The accumulator has been closed</li>\n760:      * </ul>\n761:      * </ol>\n762:      */\n763:     public ReadyCheckResult ready(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs) {\n764:         Set<Node> readyNodes = new HashSet<>();\n765:         long nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n766:         Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics = new HashSet<>();\n767:         // Go topic by topic so that we can get queue sizes for partitions in a topic and calculate\n768:         // cumulative frequency table (used in partitioner).\n769:         for (Map.Entry<String, TopicInfo> topicInfoEntry : this.topicInfoMap.entrySet()) {\n770:             final String topic = topicInfoEntry.getKey();\n771:             nextReadyCheckDelayMs = partitionReady(metadataSnapshot, nowMs, topic, topicInfoEntry.getValue(), nextReadyCheckDelayMs, readyNodes, unknownLeaderTopics);\n772:         }\n773:         return new ReadyCheckResult(readyNodes, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, unknownLeaderTopics);\n774:     }\n775: \n776:     /**\n777:      * Check whether there are any batches which haven't been drained\n778:      */\n779:     public boolean hasUndrained() {\n780:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\n781:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\n782:                 synchronized (deque) {\n783:                     if (!deque.isEmpty())\n784:                         return true;\n785:                 }\n786:             }\n787:         }\n788:         return false;\n789:     }\n790: \n791:     private boolean shouldBackoff(boolean hasLeaderChanged, final ProducerBatch batch, final long waitedTimeMs) {\n792:         boolean shouldWaitMore = batch.attempts() > 0 && waitedTimeMs < retryBackoff.backoff(batch.attempts() - 1);\n793:         boolean shouldBackoff = !hasLeaderChanged && shouldWaitMore;\n794:         if (log.isTraceEnabled()) {\n795:             if (shouldBackoff) {\n796:                 log.trace(\n797:                     \"For {}, will backoff\", batch);\n798:             } else {\n799:                 log.trace(\n800:                     \"For {}, will not backoff, shouldWaitMore {}, hasLeaderChanged {}\", batch,\n801:                     shouldWaitMore, hasLeaderChanged);\n802:             }\n803:         } else if (log.isDebugEnabled() && hasLeaderChanged) {\n804:             // Add less-verbose log at DEBUG.\n805:             log.debug(\"For {}, leader has changed, hence skipping backoff.\", batch);\n806:         }\n807:         return shouldBackoff;\n808:     }\n809: \n810:     private boolean shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(ProducerBatch first, TopicPartition tp) {\n811:         ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch;\n812:         if (transactionManager != null) {\n813:             if (!transactionManager.isSendToPartitionAllowed(tp))\n814:                 return true;\n815: \n816:             producerIdAndEpoch = transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch();\n817:             if (!producerIdAndEpoch.isValid())\n818:                 // we cannot send the batch until we have refreshed the producer id\n819:                 return true;\n820: \n821:             if (!first.hasSequence()) {\n822:                 if (transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(tp) && transactionManager.hasStaleProducerIdAndEpoch(tp)) {\n823:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the partition has in-flight batches with a different epoch\n824:                     // and/or producer ID. Otherwise, a batch with a new epoch and sequence number\n825:                     // 0 could be written before earlier batches complete, which would cause out of sequence errors\n826:                     return true;\n827:                 }\n828: \n829:                 if (transactionManager.hasUnresolvedSequence(first.topicPartition))\n830:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the state of previous sequence numbers\n831:                     // is unknown. The previous batches would be unknown if they were aborted\n832:                     // on the client after being sent to the broker at least once.\n833:                     return true;\n834:             }\n835: \n836:             int firstInFlightSequence = transactionManager.firstInFlightSequence(first.topicPartition);\n837:             // If the queued batch already has an assigned sequence, then it is being retried.\n838:             // In this case, we wait until the next immediate batch is ready and drain that.\n839:             // We only move on when the next in line batch is complete (either successfully or due to\n840:             // a fatal broker error). This effectively reduces our in flight request count to 1.\n841:             return firstInFlightSequence != RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE && first.hasSequence()\n842:                     && first.baseSequence() != firstInFlightSequence;\n843:         }\n844:         return false;\n845:     }\n846: \n847:     private List<ProducerBatch> drainBatchesForOneNode(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Node node, int maxSize, long now) {\n848:         int size = 0;\n849:         List<PartitionInfo> parts = metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForNode(node.id());\n850:         List<ProducerBatch> ready = new ArrayList<>();\n851:         if (parts.isEmpty())\n852:             return ready;\n853:         /* to make starvation less likely each node has it's own drainIndex */\n854:         int drainIndex = getDrainIndex(node.idString());\n855:         int start = drainIndex = drainIndex % parts.size();\n856:         do {\n857:             PartitionInfo part = parts.get(drainIndex);\n858: \n859:             TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(part.topic(), part.partition());\n860:             updateDrainIndex(node.idString(), drainIndex);\n861:             drainIndex = (drainIndex + 1) % parts.size();\n862:             // Only proceed if the partition has no in-flight batches.\n863:             if (isMuted(tp))\n864:                 continue;\n865:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getDeque(tp);\n866:             if (deque == null)\n867:                 continue;\n868: \n869:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(tp);\n870: \n871:             final ProducerBatch batch;\n872:             synchronized (deque) {\n873:                 // invariant: !isMuted(tp,now) && deque != null\n874:                 ProducerBatch first = deque.peekFirst();\n875:                 if (first == null)\n876:                     continue;\n877: \n878:                 // first != null\n879:                 // Only drain the batch if it is not during backoff period.\n880:                 first.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\n881:                 if (shouldBackoff(first.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), first, first.waitedTimeMs(now)))\n882:                     continue;\n883: \n884:                 if (size + first.estimatedSizeInBytes() > maxSize && !ready.isEmpty()) {\n885:                     // there is a rare case that a single batch size is larger than the request size due to\n886:                     // compression; in this case we will still eventually send this batch in a single request\n887:                     break;\n888:                 } else {\n889:                     if (shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(first, tp))\n890:                         break;\n891:                 }\n892: \n893:                 batch = deque.pollFirst();\n894: \n895:                 boolean isTransactional = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isTransactional();\n896:                 ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch =\n897:                     transactionManager != null ? transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch() : null;\n898:                 if (producerIdAndEpoch != null && !batch.hasSequence()) {\n899:                     // If the producer id/epoch of the partition do not match the latest one\n900:                     // of the producer, we update it and reset the sequence. This should be\n901:                     // only done when all its in-flight batches have completed. This is guarantee\n902:                     // in `shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition`.\n903:                     transactionManager.maybeUpdateProducerIdAndEpoch(batch.topicPartition);\n904: \n905:                     // If the batch already has an assigned sequence, then we should not change the producer id and\n906:                     // sequence number, since this may introduce duplicates. In particular, the previous attempt\n907:                     // may actually have been accepted, and if we change the producer id and sequence here, this\n908:                     // attempt will also be accepted, causing a duplicate.\n909:                     //\n910:                     // Additionally, we update the next sequence number bound for the partition, and also have\n911:                     // the transaction manager track the batch so as to ensure that sequence ordering is maintained\n912:                     // even if we receive out of order responses.\n913:                     batch.setProducerState(producerIdAndEpoch, transactionManager.sequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition), isTransactional);\n914:                     transactionManager.incrementSequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition, batch.recordCount);\n915:                     log.debug(\"Assigned producerId {} and producerEpoch {} to batch with base sequence \" +\n916:                             \"{} being sent to partition {}\", producerIdAndEpoch.producerId,\n917:                         producerIdAndEpoch.epoch, batch.baseSequence(), tp);\n918: \n919:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\n920:                 }\n921:             }\n922: \n923:             // the rest of the work by processing outside the lock\n924:             // close() is particularly expensive\n925:             batch.close();\n926:             size += batch.records().sizeInBytes();\n927:             ready.add(batch);\n928: \n929:             batch.drained(now);\n930:         } while (start != drainIndex);\n931:         return ready;\n932:     }\n933: \n934:     private int getDrainIndex(String idString) {\n935:         return nodesDrainIndex.computeIfAbsent(idString, s -> 0);\n936:     }\n937: \n938:     private void updateDrainIndex(String idString, int drainIndex) {\n939:         nodesDrainIndex.put(idString, drainIndex);\n940:     }\n941: \n942:     /**\n943:      * Drain all the data for the given nodes and collate them into a list of batches that will fit\n944:      * within the specified size on a This method attempts to avoid choosing the same\n945:      * topic-node over and over.\n946:      *\n947:      * @param metadataSnapshot  The current cluster metadata\n948:      * @param nodes             The list of node to drain\n949:      * @param maxSize           The maximum number of bytes to drain\n950:      * @param now               The current unix time in milliseconds\n951:      * @return A list of {@link ProducerBatch} for each node specified with total size less than the\n952:      * requested maxSize.\n953:      */\n954:     public Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> drain(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Set<Node> nodes, int maxSize, long now) {\n955:         if (nodes.isEmpty())\n956:             return Collections.emptyMap();\n957: \n958:         Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = new HashMap<>();\n959:         for (Node node : nodes) {\n960:             List<ProducerBatch> ready = drainBatchesForOneNode(metadataSnapshot, node, maxSize, now);\n961:             batches.put(node.id(), ready);\n962:         }\n963:         return batches;\n964:     }\n965: \n966:     public void updateNodeLatencyStats(Integer nodeId, long nowMs, boolean canDrain) {\n967:         // Don't bother with updating stats if the feature is turned off.\n968:         if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs <= 0)\n969:             return;\n970: \n971:         // When the sender gets a node (returned by the ready() function) that has data to send\n972:         // but the node is not ready (and so we cannot drain the data), we only update the\n973:         // ready time, then the difference would reflect for how long a node wasn't ready\n974:         // to send the data.   /**\n223:      * Complete the batch exceptionally.
